  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_54ae604d-f569-4155-a2a0-2d8f1101bf8e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer7147085562512596761">Clea Raymond has felt the glare of the spotlight her entire life. The daughter of a renowned surgeon and a prominent Washington DC politician, she has grown to be a talented photojournalist who takes refuge in a career that allows her to travel to the most exotic parts of the world. But after Clea’s father disappears while on a humanitarian mission, Clea’s photos begin to </span>
  <span id="freeText7147085562512596761" style="display:none">Clea Raymond has felt the glare of the spotlight her entire life. The daughter of a renowned surgeon and a prominent Washington DC politician, she has grown to be a talented photojournalist who takes refuge in a career that allows her to travel to the most exotic parts of the world. But after Clea’s father disappears while on a humanitarian mission, Clea’s photos begin to feature eerie, shadowy images of a strange and beautiful man—a man she has never seen before.<br /><br />When fate brings Clea and this man together, she is stunned by the immediate and powerful connection she feels with him. As they grow closer, they are drawn deep into the mystery behind her father’s disappearance, and they discover the centuries old truth behind their intense bond. Torn by a dangerous love triangle and haunted by a powerful secret that holds their fates, together they race against time to unravel their pasts in order to save their lives—and their futures.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_124004433" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124004433" />
    <a title="Morgan F" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2941288-morgan-f"><img alt="Morgan F" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262298598p2/2941288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124004433?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morgan F" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morgan F" href="/user/show/2941288-morgan-f">Morgan F</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=terrible-parents">terrible-parents</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=its-a-girl">its-a-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=pulse-it">pulse-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=debut">debut</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124004433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4653141783088344074">I'm warning you now. This is more of a rant than a cohesive, intelligent review. It will be filled with spoilers and un-ladylike language, so people of delicate sensibilities take heed.<br/><br/>I like Hilary Duff. I grew up with her in Lizzie Maguire, and even rocked the Lizzie hairstyle for a while. I think she has grown into a nice young starlet as opposed to, well, <a href='http://img.perezhilton.com/wp-content/uploads/2007/07/mugshot__oPt.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>this</i>
</a><br/><br/>I was curious about this book after seeing her name on it. I was interested. How much of it did Hilary actually write? Did she jus</span>
  <span id="freeText4653141783088344074" style="display:none">I'm warning you now. This is more of a rant than a cohesive, intelligent review. It will be filled with spoilers and un-ladylike language, so people of delicate sensibilities take heed.<br /><br />I like Hilary Duff. I grew up with her in Lizzie Maguire, and even rocked the Lizzie hairstyle for a while. I think she has grown into a nice young starlet as opposed to, well, <a href="http://img.perezhilton.com/wp-content/uploads/2007/07/mugshot__oPt.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>this</i>
</a><br /><br />I was curious about this book after seeing her name on it. I was interested. How much of it did Hilary actually write? Did she just tell Elise Allen "write about soulmates" and then go and get a manicure? Or did she come up with plot herself, with Elise Allen only writing it down on paper? I think, after reading it, that I know the answer. I believe this is how the conception of this book transpired: <br /><br />Hilary's manager walks into Borders mistakenly, absolutely absorbed into keying things into his Blackberry. It is only when he walks into a table, toppling over a pile of books, that he looks up and acknowledges his surroundings. <i>Hey! This isn't Saks!</i> But then his eye is drawn to a picture of Lauren Conrad on the back of Sweet Little Lies. He smirks, because he has his suspicions how much of the book Lauren actually wrote. Surprisingly, he sees multiple teenagers in the check-out line with the book in hand. <i> Hmmpp</i>, he thinks, <i> Hilary is ten times prettier and smarter and nicer than LC</i> Then a brilliant idea forms in his head. Hilary's name + YA book = new sports car. Excitedly, he gathers a copy of every YA book in the store and rushes back to the office to make some phone calls. <i>Hey, Hilary, babe….how would you like to write the ultimate YA book?</i><br /><br />Next time, Hilary, just say no. <br /><br />This book infuriated me. How stupid do publishers think teens are? This is the same typical formula for every other YA paranormal book out there, except wrapped up in a different dress. <br /><br />There was nothing special about it. No spark. The writing was dead and lifeless, as were all the characters. I was bored out of my mind with the predictability of it all when I wasn't in a rage of seething hot fury. <br /><br />Clea Raymond, the narrator, is horrible. She has no personality, and nothing that distinguishes her from every other YA heroine out there. Her name is also too close to "Claire" for my liking, and those of you who've read my other rants know my reasoning for that. Clea is a stupid, vapid girl, who became absolutely insufferable after she discovered *ahem* <i>tru wuv</i>. That's right, folks, she has a <i>soulmate</i>. But don't be too jealous of her now. She also has the inexplicable burden of being caught in the middle of a love triangle. What would a YA book be without one of those? Of course, Clea had no idea her BFF Ben, had feelings for her until he started being a jealous prick. Clea, you give a bad name to women everywhere. We are girls. We <i>always</i> know. Platonic friends, my ass.<br /><br />Of course, I could have forgiven the book for this. Love triangles are a staple because they create drama and act as filler. Except this one was so blatantly one-sided. We all know Clea lllllluuuuuurrrrvvvvessss Sage (her soulmate guy), who is also immortal. Clea herself is kind of immortal, but more on that later. I might be spoiling things a little here, but suck it up. I'm trying to save you here. Clea and Sage had known each other less than a week. At first, Clea thought he was a crazy stalker. Then she thought he was a serial killer deadset on sending her to the grave. Then all the sudden they were kissing, telling each other how much they loved each other, and having sex in a car. First off, if a guy (with the exception of Leonardo DiCaprio) lets you lose your virginity in car, he does not really love you. Second off, this guy has been around for 500 years. Do you know how many STDs he could have contracted in that time? I don't care if he's immortal. As my health teacher said, herpes can affect anybody. And lastly, WTF CLEA?!! You have known this guy <i>one week</i> and up until a few hours ago you thought he was going to kill you!!!!!!! WHY! And then of course, from then on, it causes her physical pain to be away from her Sagey-poo. Gag me.<br /><br />I blame Clea's whore friend, Rayna. Rayna, as Clea describes her, is a "romantic" who finds a new "soulmate" everytime she leaves the house. There are words for those kinds of girls, so don't go beating around the bush. Anyway, Rayna gives Clea the <i>poetic</i> advice of "don't think, just feel" right before Clea goes off alone with Sage, the soulmate/stranger/serial killer. NO NO NO. Think first, Clea, think first!! Do you <i>want</i> to become a statistic? This book is all your fault, Rayna, and I hate you. <br /><br />When everyone wasn't talking about soulmates, they were trying to figure out the mystery of where Clea's father disappeared to. Of course, the focus of the book turned to Sage as soon as he appeared. But anyway, the beginning was rather slow, but then everything happened like BAM!BAM!BAM!. Any information the reader found out was in clumps under circumstances that were too convenient for my liking. It was frustrating. A part I did enjoy was all of Clea's past lives, but those were clumped up and rushed. I think it would have been better to have them dispersed throughout the novel. The ending was also extremely abrupt with so many questions unanswered, I wanted to punch a baby at first. But then I realized the book was over, so then I felt happy again. Here are a list of my questions/complaints:<br /><br />1. Does Clea not have to go to school? I'm not sure what time of the year this book is taking place, but Clea is still able to drop everything and go to South America or Japan whenever she feels like it. With only two boys for company. <br />2. Why do people in Japan know who Clea is? Since when is being a senator's daughter such a flippin' big deal that people on the other side of the world know who you are? I don't even know my Senators' names. <br />3. Why is Clea's mother so horrible? She just let's Clea have total independence. Want to go to Peru? Go ahead! Guam? Why not! Afghanistan? Be sure to bring lots of sunscreen! And you would think, her daughter apparently being such a big deal and all, she might have Clea assigned a body guard or something? Nope.<br />4. Why does Clea love Sage? He has no personality. She literally just decides she loves him. They didn't even have great chemistry. <br />5. Why are Clea and Ben immortal too? I understand Sage, somewhat, since he drank the elixir. But there is not explanation for Clea and Ben to have their souls being reborn again and again, and at random intervals.<br />6. What's a soul? I know what <i>my</i> definition of a soul is, but this book has me all confused. Why is Clea so talented in some lives, like being a singer, artist, or actress, but has no apparent talent in this life? Does a soul just mean you have the same personality (or lack of it)?<br />7. Why does Sage show up in Clea's pictures? Why is he sometimes floating and sometimes not? GAH NO SENSE<br />8. Is this the only time Clea is aware of her past lives?, or has she had the same dreams in her past?<br />9. Since Ben always seems to be the problem, why don't they just KILL HIM? There, problem solved. See you again in another hundred years.<br /><br />I'm just so <i>done</i> with these crappy YA paranormals. They are all the same. My intelligence is being insulted. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4653141783088344074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11708068847220738324">Let me start off by saying that I actually like Hilary, and when I found out that she wrote a YA book, I was excited.<br/><br/>Little did I know this was going to be nothing but a rip-off.<br/><br/>As I was reading this book, I realized that the similarities with Evermore were painfully obvious. Girl meets boy, girl finds out boy is immortal and has been with her in past lives, girl dies horribly every time, girl has a friend that's in love with her and jealous of the boy, boy had a past love interest that apparent</span>
  <span id="freeText11708068847220738324" style="display:none">Let me start off by saying that I actually like Hilary, and when I found out that she wrote a YA book, I was excited.<br><br>Little did I know this was going to be nothing but a rip-off.<br><br>As I was reading this book, I realized that the similarities with Evermore were painfully obvious. Girl meets boy, girl finds out boy is immortal and has been with her in past lives, girl dies horribly every time, girl has a friend that's in love with her and jealous of the boy, boy had a past love interest that apparently was a "red-haired vixen" (which, in Evermore, the bitch girl Drina also is a redhead).<br><br>I would say this, though. Clea didn't annoy me as much as Ever did. Clea didn't spend chapter after chapter pining and moaning over how muscular Sage is. Sure she'd think about him from time to time, cause that's what she was supposed to do. But she wasn't as clingy and desperate as Ever was. At least not in the first parts.<br><br>But unfortunately, further into the book she started to obsess over him. And the sex scene happened way too soon. WAY. TOO. SOON. Like, seriously. And they do it in the passenger's seat of a car.<br><br>Let me break it down for you guys:<br><br>Clea: I see you in my dreams.<br>Sage: I know. Your soul leads me to you. I love you.<br>Clea: Oh Sage, I love you too. Pop my cherry.<br>Sage: *pulls out condoms* I bought them earlier. I knew you'd be an easy target.<br>Clea: Oh, Sage.<br>Sage: Oh, Clea.<br>Clea: SAGE!<br>Sage: CLEA!<br>*explosion of pleasure*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380345610ra/700245.gif" height="235" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I wouldn't say this book was better than Evermore, but I also wouldn't say Evermore was better than this. They're equally bad. But comparing Clea to Ever, I would say Ever wins in the most brain dead category.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Also, at the end Clea calls the Savior people and gets Sage kidnapped. She should've just let him kill himself and free them of this stupid piece of shit cycle/curse/whatever. And I don't get why Ben blames himself. And I don't get why CLEA blames HIM. It doesn't matter if he ran down the hill or not. Sage would've still been kidnapped either way. That whole blaming thing really pissed me the hell off because in reality it was NOBODY'S FAULT. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Overall, this book was a hot mess. The "romance" was too cliche and sped up, and the book was overloaded with Evermore similarities. Heck, Clea and Sage even LOOK like Ever and Damen in the new paperback cover.<br><br>I thought about reading the second one, but after finding out that there will be a female character stealing Sage's attention, I was like "Fuck that." Not only because scenarios like that bother me, but because that's another similarity with the Immortals series. In the second book, the hero's off with some other bitch while flaunting it in the heroine's face.<br><br>Sadly, a lot of YA is like that these days. :/ I don't get it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345610i/700246.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm done. I think.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13805817837132711117">Bahaha, Hilary Duff wrote a book. And it was … not very good. Shocking!<br/><br/>I feel like these YA paranormal fantasy books are all the same. Nothing new ever happens! Recycled plots, with different names & different paranormal abilities! There is one boring vapid girl who is best friends with a great guy but then meets a tall, dark & mysterious stranger.   <span id="freeText13805817837132711117" style="display:none">Bahaha, Hilary Duff wrote a book. And it was … not very good. Shocking!<br /><br />I feel like these YA paranormal fantasy books are all the same. Nothing new ever happens! Recycled plots, with different names &amp; different paranormal abilities! There is one boring vapid girl who is best friends with a great guy but then meets a tall, dark &amp; mysterious stranger. Boring Vapid Girl falls instantly, madly, <i>passionately</i> in love with Tall Dark Mysterious Guy, while Great Best Friend Guy turns into a jealous jerk because He Loved Her First. Add in some immortality and paranormal activity and guys saving vapid girl from her stupidity and maybe some woe-y “Oh gosh, don’t ever leave me, I hope he doesn't leave me, WHY IS HE IGNORING ME, we are ~soulmates, I can’t live without him!!11!” and BAM! You’ve now just read 95% of all YA novels currently being published. <br /><br />My brain bleeds, BLEEDS!</span>

<div id="review_125900509" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125900509" />
    <a title="Sierra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4267600-sierra"><img alt="Sierra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303309690p2/4267600.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125900509?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sierra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sierra" href="/user/show/4267600-sierra">Sierra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125900509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16677437162274458260">When you think of Hilary Duff, you automatically think 'Lizzie McGuire', right? So, it's probably weird for you to think that she's written a book--well, at least, I did. <br/> Elixir was captivating, and not anything that I'd imagine Hilary Duff could write. I'm not dissing her, but it's just that I thought this would be some stupid story about a snobby-rich girl. True, the main character, Clea, was rich, but I didn't get the sense that she was snobby at all. <br/> She was a pretty cool protagonist, and </span>
  <span id="freeText16677437162274458260" style="display:none">When you think of Hilary Duff, you automatically think 'Lizzie McGuire', right? So, it's probably weird for you to think that she's written a book--well, at least, I did. <br /> Elixir was captivating, and not anything that I'd imagine Hilary Duff could write. I'm not dissing her, but it's just that I thought this would be some stupid story about a snobby-rich girl. True, the main character, Clea, was rich, but I didn't get the sense that she was snobby at all. <br /> She was a pretty cool protagonist, and I liked her rational-way of thinking. To be honest, she thought things out more thoroughly than I would have! Me, I would have jumped and freaked at just about every turn of events (I mean, taking a snapshot of your room and seeing some strange dude standing in your closet would have me screaming like a banshee and running out of the house).<br /> True, the story line kind of reminded me of Alyson Noel’s Immortals series a little bit, but I filed all my negative comments away, in order to stop comparing all the characters. <br /> The book was entrancing, and I finished it in under a day. I enjoyed it through-and-through, and although the ending is a little disappointing, I think there is going to be a second one in the near future (although I can't find any information on it...yet).<br /> I suggest that every person who likes strange tales of love give this book a try. Set aside your views/opinions on the new author, and give her a shot (without envisioning Lizzie Maguire’s little animated character writing this book on an overly-sized computer).<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16677437162274458260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_315737743" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/315737743" />
    <a title="Merary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6508812-merary"><img alt="Merary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483176424p2/6508812.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/315737743?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merary" href="/user/show/6508812-merary">Merary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=where-s-the-fucking-conflict">where-s-the-fucking-conflict</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=celebrity-writing">celebrity-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=it-was-okay">it-was-okay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=boring-bland-main-characters">boring-bland-main-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=guilty-pleasures">guilty-pleasures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=abusive-relationships">abusive-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=rich-and-or-famous">rich-and-or-famous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=mary-sues">mary-sues</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer315737743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer634191033193721119">What do you think when you hear the name <i>Hilary Duff</i>? Do you think of Disney's show <i>Lizzie McGuire</i> and/or her other movies? Or do you think of her 4 released albums, with her catchy songs and small, yet pretty voice?<br/>What about her novel?<br/><br/>*record scratch* <br/><br/>What? Did I just say that Hilary Duff is an <b>author</b>? Sadly, it is true. Hilary Duff wrote a novel and her book <i>Elixir</i> is now a New York Times Best Seller.<br/>Cue the disbelief.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380375563ra/730162.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>When my Drama class teacher started reading the first two pages at loud, I </span>
  <span id="freeText634191033193721119" style="display:none">What do you think when you hear the name <i>Hilary Duff</i>? Do you think of Disney's show <i>Lizzie McGuire</i> and/or her other movies? Or do you think of her 4 released albums, with her catchy songs and small, yet pretty voice?<br>What about her novel?<br><br>*record scratch* <br><br>What? Did I just say that Hilary Duff is an <b>author</b>? Sadly, it is true. Hilary Duff wrote a novel and her book <i>Elixir</i> is now a New York Times Best Seller.<br>Cue the disbelief.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380375563ra/730162.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When my Drama class teacher started reading the first two pages at loud, I had a feeling that this book was going to be terrible. The writing was very over-dramatic and exaggerated, and it almost sounded . . . sexual. And unintentionally funny. Very unintentionally funny. <br>Was I right? Hmmm . . . I'll tell you about that later.<br><br>First, I'm going to list you the <b>MAIN</b> reason why I didn't like it.<br>It is WAY too similar to <i>Evermore</i> from <i>The Immortals</i> series by Alyson Noel. <br>And if you had read my previous reviews, you are aware of my deep hatred for the series.<br>When I was reading I noticed a lot of similarities with the series and I wondered if Hilary Duff took the series as an inspiration for her book.<br><br>Before you get mad at me, I'm going to tell you that I'm very aware that Alyson Noel doesn't own immortals, in fact the subject of immortality in fiction came from the very beginning of literature and it's not new, but the similarities of <i>The Immortals</i> and <i>Elixir</i> are not just about the paranormal aspects; it is also about the male protagonists being old and creepy but considered hot and mysterious, the heroines being dumb and stupid but considered perfect, the reincarnation of the heroines in other lives for centuries, a red-haired ex who kills the reincarnations of the protagonist repeatedly, the love triangles between the mythological being and the heroines' best friend, and, of course, the sudden insta-love between the main characters.<br><br><b>The Plot</b>: It was actually a very promising plot. Clea Raymond is the daughter of famous politician mother and a surgeon father. She's also famous on her own, being a photojournalist and all. Then, a man starts appearing in her pictures, including the ones when she was a baby. And somehow, that mysterious man has a connection with the disappearance of her father. It sounded so gripping and disturbing that I actually couldn't wait to read it. My mistake. The plot was as absurd as BP's credibility. <br><br><b>The Characters</b>: I consider Clea Raymond a Mary Sue. She's rich, beautiful, popular, smart, talented, has the best two best friends in the world, she always gets what she wants, her mother is cool with whatever she does, etc. She was very boring. And whiny. Really whiny. And DAMN!! She always questions EVERYTHING! There was always questions(lots of it) in every single page! Did this happen, why it happened, could this be, would this, would that, how it happened, and freaking <b>DID MY DAD HAD A COFFIN?</b> Is she really that clueless about what's going on around her?!! I felt that I was reading <b>DORA THE FUCKING EXPLORER!!</b> And I was the audience.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380375563ra/730163.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Rayna is Clea's best friend since they were in their mother's womb (I'm not kidding). She's a romantic and believes every guy she meets is her soulmate. In other words, she's a slut. And then, there's Ben (the only one with a normal name), Clea's best friend/bodyguard. He is in love with Clea but she doesn't acknowledge that. Don't worry, she will.<br><br><b>The Man in the Pictures</b>: The creepy, old man that Clea first suspected as a murderer. Or an incubus that wanted to impregnate her with a demon child. Then, as a guardian angel and soulmate. UGH. Serve me up, insta-love! And the 600-year-old immortal's name is. . . Sage.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/289387.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Seriously, that's his name! Can't. Stop. Laughing. HAHAHAHA!! Sage reminds me of a pornstar, even the name of an overly sexual little girl. Or a drag queen. <br><br>I had many problems with this book: There's no chemistry between Clea and Sage. There's no explanation for their attraction. None. Rayna is annoying. Clea's mother is very careless: "You want to go to Tokyo, Brazil, Europe or whatever place you want? Here's my credit card, have fun!" And, does she EVER go to school? She's SEVENTEEN years old! I remember in one chapter that Clea told Rayna to stay home because she has school the next day. And Clea apparently isn't home-schooled or has a tutor, so I assume that Clea doesn't go to school. . . at all. When Sage finally tells Clea about their soulmate status, she loses her virginity with him in the back of Rayna's car! They'd only met for 2 days! And he already had a condom with him! EWW!!! Disgusting! And the next day, he ignores her. He might as well told her this:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380375563ra/730165.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don't feel sorry for her.<br>And I blame Rayna for what happened (She's the one who told Clea not to think).<br><br>The book was dull. There's no real conflict. It was plain, brainless, stupid, moronic. But heck, I was entertained by the stupidity of it. <br><br>Her writing was alright, though. No grammar or punctuation mistakes. But it was very juvenile. I felt that a teenager wrote this instead of a 20+ year old woman.<br><br>But then . . . the climax reached. The last two chapters were actually the only good parts of this whole book and the cliffhanger was good enough to continue with the sequel. It was like, Duff (or Elise Allen) finally woke up and thought of writing the story well. But it didn't last long. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Sage was actually suicidal and when he got kidnapped, Clea blames it on Ben, which is bad enough because he feels that it was all his fault. Now she has to rescue her "soulmate". <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>In conclusion: The writing was ok, but the book was very flawed in characters and plot. Almost cheesy and ridiculous. It was better than the last YA paranormal novels that have been released (e.g. <i>Twilight</i>, <i>The Immortals</i>), but it wasn't good enough to even be considered unique and great. And not bad enough to be on my shelf of "Worst Books I'd Ever Read".<br><br>I'm going to read the sequel, anyways.<br><br>(By the way, I wrote the review listening to Hilary Duff's music. Because I'm weird like that.)</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="634191033193721119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/679025-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323234939p2/679025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_146401758" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146401758" />
    <a title="Picture  Perfect" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3517393-picture-perfect"><img alt="Picture  Perfect" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395197093p2/3517393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146401758?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Picture  Perfect" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Picture  Perfect" href="/user/show/3517393-picture-perfect">Picture  Perfect</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Dumb Airheads who don't care about writing at all. </span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer146401758&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146401758" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2677546722008113531">I didn't have high hopes for this book when I read this book. I actually wanted to prove that I was right in the sense that this book would "suck". And, it did. It sucked guts. From the first page, the book lost my attention. The font was pretty big for a novel. Of course, that's just the beginning of it all. Here is my list of unfathomable things about this book: <br/><br/>1. The size of the font. Who is she kidding? Could she not fill up the book?<br/>2. Many grammatical errors. I didn't find and pinpoint al</span>
  <span id="freeText2677546722008113531" style="display:none">I didn't have high hopes for this book when I read this book. I actually wanted to prove that I was right in the sense that this book would "suck". And, it did. It sucked guts. From the first page, the book lost my attention. The font was pretty big for a novel. Of course, that's just the beginning of it all. Here is my list of unfathomable things about this book: <br /><br />1. The size of the font. Who is she kidding? Could she not fill up the book?<br />2. Many grammatical errors. I didn't find and pinpoint all of them because I don't like to do that. But, some were just so easy to catch. <br />3. Clichéd plot. Totally copied Evermore by Alyson Noel. Alyson Noel should sue. It kind of brought all of the "Immortal series" books into one book to start off Hilary Duff's series. <br />In both books, there is an immortal character. An elixir. A conflicting character between the romance. This book doesn't talk about powers or anything. But, it does mention at the end the "forbidden relationship". Comparing this book to Evermore is actually not an accomplishment. <br />4. I totally wanted to slam the book against the wall. Hilary Duff watches too many movies. Way too many. So, Clea meets her "soulmate" in a span of 2-3 days. Declares that she loves with him and is the man in her dreams. And, when she is supposed to be picking up snacks, she has sex...with him...in the passenger seat...of her best friend's car. Talk about wrong. That is not romantic. I think that's kind of...weird, considering how Sage happened to bring along birth control. EWWWWW!!! This series should totally end with Clea getting some rare immortal STD from Sage. Ha. <br />5. The romance between Clea and Sage is really weird and bi-polar. It's lust not love. <br />6. The characters are very weakly-developed. In the beginning, Clea basically acted like some storyteller. Randomly, she started thinking about her life...in a nightclub. <br />7. The plot dragged on at some parts but sped in some parts. It's like Hilary Duff just wanted to write for the sake of finishing a book and getting publicity. Hilary Duff! Don't quit your day job! Wait, I think she doesn't even have one. Last time I checked, her acting career disappeared. <br /><br /><br />Anyway, despite all the negative comments, the book was decent probably because Hilary Duff had some help from another person and all. I think it should be Elise Allen with Hilary Duff. But, I can tell that Hilary Duff did think of the story. She must have read Evermore before writing. Ha. The humor is kind of strange and some parts. It's okay if you like Twilight and all. The writing was pretty poor and boring. I kind of feel Tokyo and Conneticut and Brazil are the same place now. A good writer would have put description into the quickly-changing setting. It may seem excess, but it isn't. It gives the plot more of an even tempo which is totally lacking in this book. I will not read the rest of the series.<br /><br />-Picture Perfect<br /></span>

<div id="review_143981479" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143981479" />
    <a title="Reading Teen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3329955-reading-teen"><img alt="Reading Teen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294347905p2/3329955.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143981479?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading Teen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading Teen" href="/user/show/3329955-reading-teen">Reading Teen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143981479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15575381146748681446">When I first picked this book up, I laughed.<br/>Because I really could not believe that Hilary Duff had written a YA book.<br/>I grew up being a huge fan of Lizzie Mcguire and loving Hilary's CD's through my<br/>pre-teen years.<br/>So I thought, "What the heck. I'll read it."<br/>I found myself being completely surprised with how good it was.<br/>I was expecting something a little like:<br/>"Well there is like, a tree.<br/>And it's like, purple.<br/>There are like, purple leaves on this like, tree."<br/>The book was nothing like that.<br/>It was ac</span>
  <span id="freeText15575381146748681446" style="display:none">When I first picked this book up, I laughed.<br />Because I really could not believe that Hilary Duff had written a YA book.<br />I grew up being a huge fan of Lizzie Mcguire and loving Hilary's CD's through my<br />pre-teen years.<br />So I thought, "What the heck. I'll read it."<br />I found myself being completely surprised with how good it was.<br />I was expecting something a little like:<br />"Well there is like, a tree.<br />And it's like, purple.<br />There are like, purple leaves on this like, tree."<br />The book was nothing like that.<br />It was actually well written.<br />But part of me wonders how much of the book Hilary Duff wrote.<br />But then I feel kinda guilty for actually thinking that,<br />because Hilary Duff might have written the entire book,<br />and since she is an actress I'm just assuming she doesn't have a brain,<br />and decided that writing a YA novel would be "fun".<br />But you know, Hilary Duff might surprise us all and actually have a brain.<br /><br />To be honest, there were a couple parts in this book that creeped me out.<br />Because I get really creeped out by stalkers.<br />And some parts were pretty darn violent.<br />I guess little miss Lizzie Mcguire has a dark side to her.<br /><br />Even though I really liked this book,<br />and it kept me thoroughly entertained for the 3 days it took me to read it.<br />I (of course) have a complaint,<br />I thought it was kinda silly how easily Clea fell for Sage.<br />I mean, one second she is sure he is going to kill her,<br />and the next she is making out with him in her car.<br />If I was sketchy about some dude killing me,<br />I would not fall in love with him.<br />But maybe all this ranting is because I didn't really like Sage.<br />Nope, I really enjoyed Ben.<br />I wanted Clea to get with Ben so badly!<br />But then again, it probably will happen in the (I'm assuming) second book.<br />Because that would be the cliche thing to do.<br />And well, yes, I am assuming that Hilary Duff will do something<br />completely cliche.<br />But you never know, she might just knock our socks off with this one.<br /><br />-Abigaile <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://ReadingTeen.net/">http://ReadingTeen.net/</a></span>

<div id="review_122653862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122653862" />
    <a title="Azn_seddie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4312761-azn-seddie"><img alt="Azn_seddie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533918517p2/4312761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122653862?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Azn_seddie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Azn_seddie" href="/user/show/4312761-azn-seddie">Azn_seddie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122653862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11519154031971411327"><b>*EDIT*</b> I really loved it!! The plot is definitely well-written and put together. Hilary truly had a great sense of her characters and where she wanted to story to go. I guess you could say the first chapter is a bit wordy but it's descriptive/detailed/vivid enough for the reader to imagine the scene and get to know the characters. After that, the pacing is pretty good. I'm definitely liking the dynamic between Clea and her best friends, Rayna and Ben. In a perilous situation, Clea totally lets y</span>
  <span id="freeText11519154031971411327" style="display:none"><b>*EDIT*</b> I really loved it!! The plot is definitely well-written and put together. Hilary truly had a great sense of her characters and where she wanted to story to go. I guess you could say the first chapter is a bit wordy but it's descriptive/detailed/vivid enough for the reader to imagine the scene and get to know the characters. After that, the pacing is pretty good. I'm definitely liking the dynamic between Clea and her best friends, Rayna and Ben. In a perilous situation, Clea totally lets you know how she functions with and without them. She's the more good-humored, humble, insecure of the 3 while Rayna is the ideal BFF package and Ben is the support system. There's plenty of one-liners that added a nice touch of humor between the 3, which was a good contrast to the heavier and slightly gory scenes and which made me LOL. Speaking of the more graphic scenes, I was certainly freaked out by them. The end of ch. 2 gave me the willies and Clea's nightmares gave me a good scare. So, props to Hilary for evoking fear off the pages.<br /><br />I also got a good sense of Clea's relationship with her father. Even though they were really close, there's still a huge amount of innocence that Clea ends up having to sort through and understand. I hope later on in the series, Hilary can develop Clea's relationship with her mom, depending on where the story goes cuz as of now, there's some instability and insecurity and distance that needs to eventually be addressed. As for Clea and Sage, I really liked the fact that Clea didn't let her feelings get in the way of her trying to look at their situation logically for most of the book. At first, Sage and Clea's spiritual bond comes off a bit disjointed and kind of hard to believe during the second half of the book, though I think that was partially its intention for what is revealed when they're in Japan. That's probably my only concern. Other than that, I can see why the Ben-Clea-Sage love triangle was so dangerous; I don't even know who Clea should truly be with. And I think that's good cuz Clea's been through heck and I'm waiting for some more development later in the series. And I felt that was a good place for Hilary to have the cliffhanger.<br /><br />Overall, Elixir was a quick, enjoyable read and I can't wait to see what Hilary does with book 2.<br /><br />I'm a huge Hilary fan and I think adding Author to her resume is awesome. She's told stories through her songwriting (and acting), so it seems natural for her to do the same in book form and Hilary said the same thing during her TODAY Show interview today. I also think it's cool of her to have a fiction series out instead of a memoir/autobio cuz it seems like most celebs do memoirs/autobios. Not saying that's bad, it just that it's not very often that celebs are interested in writing fiction. It's different in a good way. Hilary and Tyra are only 2 of the small handful, that I know off the top of my head, that are doing/have done this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11519154031971411327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2637037644278286654">Let me tell you a common story we see everyday in YA fiction.<br/><br/>She is seventeen. He is about 500 years old.<br/><br/>When she sees him in her photos, she believes him to be a semi-stalker/ cold-blooded killer dead set on bringing her to her grave.<br/><br/>Five minutes after meeting him, she teams up with him to find her father, putting her safety in his hands...ALL THE WHILE STILL EXTREMELY SUSPICIOUS ABOUT HIS TRUE MOTIVES.<br/><br/>A day later, she literally decides to ditch her geeky, supportive best friend whom she's know</span>
  <span id="freeText2637037644278286654" style="display:none">Let me tell you a common story we see everyday in YA fiction.<br /><br />She is seventeen. He is about 500 years old.<br /><br />When she sees him in her photos, she believes him to be a semi-stalker/ cold-blooded killer dead set on bringing her to her grave.<br /><br />Five minutes after meeting him, she teams up with him to find her father, putting her safety in his hands...ALL THE WHILE STILL EXTREMELY SUSPICIOUS ABOUT HIS TRUE MOTIVES.<br /><br />A day later, she literally decides to ditch her geeky, supportive best friend whom she's known all her life for the love of her life whom 24 hours ago, she belived he was semi-stalking her.<br /><br />A while later, she and her stalker are getting it on and gets to second base (and in her best friend's car, too). BTW, she's known him for little over two days.<br /><br />The day afterwards, he deliberately ignores her, pretending what happened between them did not, well, happen, and that leaves her beyond devasted, grief-stricken, and lifeless. Heartbroken is too nice of a word to describe how she feels. There is simply just no hope for her, no future without him.<br /><br />WELCOME TO THE WORLD OF TEEN FICTION.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/141045159" />
    <a title="Jenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2405317-jenna"><img alt="Jenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587659581p2/2405317.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/141045159?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna" href="/user/show/2405317-jenna">Jenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2405317-jenna?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2405317-jenna?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer141045159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15781212971958744723">Yes, I read the Hilary Duff novel. Because Hilary Duff is awesome, that's why. If you don't believe me, please see "The Lizzie McGuire Movie" for further proof.<br/><br/>I was very impressed with the story that Duff wove, and I devoured it like candy. Riveting right up until the end, then the abrupt/cliff-hanger type ending left me flat. I had hoped this was going to be a stand-alone book -- even if it is the first in a series.<br/><br/>And, yes, I'll read the next book when it comes out. Because Duff is actually a</span>
  <span id="freeText15781212971958744723" style="display:none">Yes, I read the Hilary Duff novel. Because Hilary Duff is awesome, that's why. If you don't believe me, please see "The Lizzie McGuire Movie" for further proof.<br /><br />I was very impressed with the story that Duff wove, and I devoured it like candy. Riveting right up until the end, then the abrupt/cliff-hanger type ending left me flat. I had hoped this was going to be a stand-alone book -- even if it is the first in a series.<br /><br />And, yes, I'll read the next book when it comes out. Because Duff is actually a pretty good storyteller. I hesitate to call her a "writer," as there is a co-writer credit on this book alongside Duff's name. So I'm not sure how much she crafted herself. But I'm positive the story is completely hers. The writing does fumble in spots, when too much dialogue trumps giving solid descriptions. I could never clearly envision the main players. Well, it's a book, after all -- perhaps I should let my imagination do some of the work.<br /><br />The story involved a privileged teen (the daughter of famous parents -- one a politician, the other a world-renowned surgeon) who has a passion for photography. After a trip to Europe, Clea finds some unsettling images in the photos she snapped. The photos are what catapult her on a scavenger hunt across the globe to find the answers from everything to the secret to immortality and the mysterious man that keeps appearing in her dreams. <br /><br />All in all, the writing flaws weren't enough to take away from its delicious story. No, there are times it doesn't make sense. Just go with it. It's a fun paranormal mystery that doesn't take itself too seriously (so I'm not going to either.) <br /><br />For reals, I can't expect any more than that.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15781212971958744723" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12409281233592114348">Seventeen year old, around the world photojournalist, Clea Raymond still misses and wonders what happened to her father who disappeared a year ago in Rio. Many things happen at once when Clea discovers an image of a man in one of her photos and then that same mysterious man lives in her dreams. Clea and her best friend Ben go to Rio and in hopes to uncover the truth about what really happen to her father and how it ties in with a man that she's always seemed to know deep in her soul...<br/><br/>I've alway</span>
  <span id="freeText12409281233592114348" style="display:none">Seventeen year old, around the world photojournalist, Clea Raymond still misses and wonders what happened to her father who disappeared a year ago in Rio. Many things happen at once when Clea discovers an image of a man in one of her photos and then that same mysterious man lives in her dreams. Clea and her best friend Ben go to Rio and in hopes to uncover the truth about what really happen to her father and how it ties in with a man that she's always seemed to know deep in her soul...<br /><br />I've always been fascinated with reincarnation and immorality in my reads and while the book concept sounds good, I couldn't love <b>Elixir</b> as much as I wanted to.<br /><br />Always liked Hilary Duff, and the writing is actually pretty good.<br />But, the characters fell flat and the pacing was off in some places and rushed in others.<br />I wish we had some more character development concerning Sage, he upset me the most actually. I thought the relationship between him and Clea moved to quickly, specially in the car, which was just ridiculous. I didn't feel any connection nor chemistry. Plus his hot and cold attitude was starting to tick me off. Also, I thought that Clea wasn't interesting enough for an MC.<br />I did however get a kick out of the dreams and the background history that was provided from them. But sadly, it's not enough to continue on with this series.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15004800222523760683">I am finally writing a review for this book.<br/><br/>I have had this book for a really long time.. I had only bought it because Hilary Duff was the author.. I didn't expect much from it, I didn't think I would like it; but I was wrong.<br/><br/>This book was so interesting..   <span id="freeText15004800222523760683" style="display:none">I am finally writing a review for this book.<br /><br />I have had this book for a really long time.. I had only bought it because Hilary Duff was the author.. I didn't expect much from it, I didn't think I would like it; but I was wrong.<br /><br />This book was so interesting.. It's definitely different from anything I've read. The whole Elixir thing was so cool, and intriguing. Each chapter was different and so much happened in each chapter. The whole story is just fast paced and so many things happen. I really like Sage! Although there's a lot that happens with him, which i'm not going to talk about. I like him as a character tho. I liked Clea as a main character she was very adamant about finding her father. The whole dreams and pictures thing with Sage was so interesting and different for me, I loved it.<br /> <br />I couldn't give this book a full 5 stars, there were just parts where I was confused or didn't care for some of the events that were happening. There's a love triangle which I hate.. Especially when the best friend is involved.. I'm not a huge fan of the best friend being in love with the main character trope anymore.. I've read too much of it. That is one of the reasons I gave it 4 stars.<br /><br />Overall it was a good book and an interesting read. I enjoyed it, but it definitely isn't for everyone. I will be continuing on with the trilogy.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3419628989718552080">I don’t know why I do this to myself; it’s like asking yourself to be bitchslapped over and over again. This book made me <i>furious</i>. Absolutely furious.<br/><br/>Clea is just stupid as hell, and if I found any person in real life like her, I’d stay far the heck away. Seriously. You know if you found a guy who showed up EVERYWHERE you went, appeared in all your pictures, and somehow you can feel his presence/see his shadow in places you go to, wouldn’t you be FREAKED the fuck out? Like holy shit, there’s som</span>
  <span id="freeText3419628989718552080" style="display:none">I don’t know why I do this to myself; it’s like asking yourself to be bitchslapped over and over again. This book made me <i>furious</i>. Absolutely furious.<br /><br />Clea is just stupid as hell, and if I found any person in real life like her, I’d stay far the heck away. Seriously. You know if you found a guy who showed up EVERYWHERE you went, appeared in all your pictures, and somehow you can feel his presence/see his shadow in places you go to, wouldn’t you be FREAKED the fuck out? Like holy shit, there’s some psychopathic lunatic or some crazy ass ghost stalking me around? You would, right? Well, no not Clea. Once she finds out it’s this epitome of hotness guy, she is head over heels for him.<br /><br />And if some guy randomly appears everywhere I am I would file a restraining order on that maggot. But no, they have to have their little conversions and she’s all drool worthy over him. And then when they actually have their first kiss he takes her to his car and TAKES AWAY HER VIRGINITY! WTF!? And when she asked him as they were getting hot and heavy that they needed to stop because you know there’s no protection in sight, he’s all I came prepared and whips out that condom. WTF. Ugh, that man isn’t in it for anything but the sex, woman!<br /><br />What’s worse is the next day, the next day; he treats her like dirt and refuses to acknowledge her presence. WTF. And don’t give me this bullshit about how they’re not meant to be together so he’s doing it for her protection crap. That is pathetic! You just took away the girl’s virginity! Some supposed soulmate you are! I absolutely hate how this book makes it seem like this is how wrapped in a neat little message that this is how real love and romance supposed to be. HELL FUCKING NO. <br /><br />I will never advocate this sort of degrading treatment of women and the pure expression of love in such a way. <i>Never.</i><br /><br />I wonder if Hilary Duff actually read this crap that was published under her name. Sure she spawned the idea for it (and what nonsense it is) but she didn’t write it. Some woman named Elise Allen did. The writing is pretty much standard fare for the genre; quick, to the point, and lacking in depth or analysis. At least the plot moved by at a quick pace, so you can just speed right through this book. It helps that the margins were absolutely HUGE. And, yes, I’m totally sure a girl can gallivant off all over the world because we’re all just so rich and her mommy would be absolutely fine with it because it’s for her daughter’s own personal freedom and expression. Get real. I would be flipping my shit if I found out my daughter was traveling all over the world without so much as a real chaperone and getting into some pretty unsafe situations. (Yeah, that 19-year-old college kid ain’t gonna do it for me.) But this is excused because a) she’s an awesome genius photographer and b) well, her mommy is some super important congressman. Hah.<br /><br />Ugh. I’m sure if you’re those readers who pick up the standard ya paranormal drivel that’s flooding the market nowadays and love them without a spec of critical thinking, you’d find this book absolutely superb. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12674261457491553464">Hilary Duff wrote this book. I was sceptical to say the least(see the pre-reading bit for more info), and now I've read it, just to see if it was as bad as people say.<br/><br/>Okay, so I just finnished this book late last night. Needless to say, it was just plain odd. I didn't like it in the slightest really. <br/><br/>It gets half a satr for plot and half a star for making me laugh, albeit unintentionally. <br/><br/><b>The Plot:</b> You know this one already. Clea is a cribbabe-playing, tea-obsessed, iris neckalce waering, photo </span>
  <span id="freeText12674261457491553464" style="display:none">Hilary Duff wrote this book. I was sceptical to say the least(see the pre-reading bit for more info), and now I've read it, just to see if it was as bad as people say.<br /><br />Okay, so I just finnished this book late last night. Needless to say, it was just plain odd. I didn't like it in the slightest really. <br /><br />It gets half a satr for plot and half a star for making me laugh, albeit unintentionally. <br /><br /><b>The Plot:</b> You know this one already. Clea is a cribbabe-playing, tea-obsessed, iris neckalce waering, photo journalistic politicatian's daughter. That's about as much as I could get from her. Nothing really huge, just minor spikes of OMG to give the appearance of a character. Well back to the plot, or lack of it anyway.<br /><br />Clea takes some photos and then some random dude starts showing up in them. Then some other crap happens and then she meets the dude in the photograph. <br /><br />His name is....SAGE! Yep, Sage. I laugh. She meets him in Brazil. And then promptly gets caught up in this whole thing involving her dad's research into the Elixr of Life. <br /><br />I won't go into any more detail, becuase if I do I'll just laugh. <br /><br /><b>The Romance:</b> Soulmates. Yep. Another one of them. You think this should be awesome right? That the whole thing will just be...amazing. But really in here it just seems like a good excuse to have sex in the front seat of the best friend's car only a day or two after meeting. <br />I mean really, what has YA lit come to? Is this what they call romantic? <br />More like it's a whoel bunch of stupid. <br /><br />I didn't really feel much for Sage other than...well nothing. I didn't have any sort of feeling for him. I didn't even care if he got himself killed. Ever. <br /><br />Also, this book is a total rip-off of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3975774.Evermore__The_Immortals___1_" title="Evermore (The Immortals, #1) by Alyson Noel" rel="nofollow noopener">Evermore</a> despite the differnces. <br /><br /><b>On Actually Reading it:</b> I really, really did laugh my way though this book. it was just that full of crap. Like the Cursed Vengance as the evil group's name. I mean really, if the name was in latin or something impressive, I might have given it a pass, but really, CV was a terrible name. I could think up better names in my sleep. <br />It got to the point where I just read it becuase I wanted to see if there were anymore lols. But then the whole car-sex came in and it just went to s**t. <br /><br /><b>The Final Verdict:</b> Unless you're a thirteen year old female trendhound, then I say stay away. I don't reccomend it. Elixr was so full of crap it coulda been a sewerage plant. So yeah, don't be like me and read it. <br /><br /><b>Pre-Reading:</b> HILARY DUFF WROTE A BOOK?<br /><br />I mean really, Duff? A Novelist?<br /><br />What is this world comming to?<br /><br />Ah well, if this book makes an appearance in my library, I'll check it out(sure as hell not buying it, duff already has enough cash, sides' there are more important books on my to-read shelf, ie all of the other ones) and after reading(if I actually finnish it....) let's see how much I wanna burn it.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12674261457491553464" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11760275752840874693" style="display:none">The people giving this book good reviews really couldn't have read the same book I did! <br /><br />OK, here are some spoilers...AKA my problems with this story.<br />-Clea's dad is missing, and has been declared dead. She's looking for him, and thinks maybe he's still alive. Nothing happens on this topic.<br />-Clea finds that in the pictures she takes there's a strange man, always in the same clothes, always in the background, never seen or noticed in real life. We later find out he's her soul-mate, and not actually there, but his soul is so drawn to her that an image of him shows up in photographs.<br />-Then we find out that her dad hired Ben, one of her two friends, because of his belief in the supernatural. Ben is in love with Clea, but she's clueless. When she tells him about the man in the photo's he shows her pictures that her father took of her throughout her life. Mystery, shadow man is in them. Her father had hired Ben to protect her, in case the shadow mystery man was an incubus. But her dad thought there was also the possibility that he was her Guardian Angel. (Are you tired of this too?)<br />-In the end, have we found out anything about daddy? No. Does anything happen with Ben, well yes! We find out that he has been the cause of Clea's death in her past four lives! How about our mystery man... Well she finds him, feels a connection to him that transcends space and time, then he gets kidnapped, because she told his enemies where he was (so tangled and ridiculous). Then she's mad at Ben because, somehow this is his fault. <br />The End. Lovely!<br /></span>

<div id="review_106467872" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106467872" />
    <a title="Connie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/630239-connie"><img alt="Connie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392873802p2/630239.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106467872?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Connie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Connie" href="/user/show/630239-connie">Connie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/630239-connie?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106467872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17060881201776238814">'Hilary Duff wrote a book?!' That was the reaction most people had when they realized what I was reading. To be honest, my reaction was the same when I first found out she was writing a YA novel. But when I read the summary, I was pleasantly surprised. It actually sounded promising. After finishing it though, I had problems with the execution of the plot and the characters. <br/><br/>One, Clea's background. Okay, so she's the daughter of a famous surgeon and a politician that has felt the spotlight her wh</span>
  <span id="freeText17060881201776238814" style="display:none">'Hilary Duff wrote a book?!' That was the reaction most people had when they realized what I was reading. To be honest, my reaction was the same when I first found out she was writing a YA novel. But when I read the summary, I was pleasantly surprised. It actually sounded promising. After finishing it though, I had problems with the execution of the plot and the characters. <br /><br />One, Clea's background. Okay, so she's the daughter of a famous surgeon and a politician that has felt the spotlight her whole life. I might buy that she grew up kind of famous, but not to the extent portrayed in the novel. The America I know is more obsessed about the children of actors, models and the like. Unless you're the president or vice-president, most of America probably won't know who their politicians' kids are. I like to think of myself as sort-of politically savvy and I don't know who my senator's kids are, much less the kids from a senator from another state. <br /><br />Two, Clea's characterization. Clea is rich, smart, famous, etc. Which probably won't be relatable to many readers. However, her sense of loss from her father's death, her drive for independence from her celebrity parent, and her strong friendship with Rayna does bridge the gap between her character and the reader's. That's a plus. However, Clea never felt completely fleshed out to me. She never becomes a three-dimensional person in my mind. I feel like with Clea and all the other characters is that Duff was just skimming the surface. There was so much to explore with these characters. But Rayna is the stock best friend. Ben is the boy who secretly crushes on her. And Sage is the mysterious boy who Clea is drawn to. <br /><br />Three, Sage and Clea's relationship. I didn't buy it. It was one of those typical YA cliché where they have an instant connection and fall in love in a span of a couple days. Yea, that didn't sit well with me. I like my romances to build up. And it's not really about the days, but the fact that you barely know anything about him. <br /><br />Four and last point, the plot. The premise was oh so promising. But there were so many plot holes. A lot of the plot seemed forced and engineered to get to where the author wanted it to be. Nothing felt natural. The home schooling is mention a continuous amount, but that was seemed like a way to explain all the jet setting all the time. And the two groups after the Elixir. They never really get explained. They become convenient villains. And a web forum?! For groups that sound like secret cults, a web forum?! Way to broadcast your not-so-secret group to the rest of the world. And the climax, a complete dud. <br /><br />I really wanted to like this book. But there were so many problems. It's an easy read, if you can get pass the undeveloped plot and 2-D characters. I couldn't.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17060881201776238814" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13647257331192041283">Elixir by Hillary Duff Book Review<br/><br/>parafantasy.blogpsot.com<br/><br/>Originality- <br/>I liked the aspect of it being about immortality, but I felt like I’ve read something like it before. Like Evermore by Allison Noel. <br/>3/5<br/><br/>Characters- <br/>I thought Clea was an okay protagonist. It was interesting to follow her side of the story but then again, I couldn’t really connect with her. <br/>I loved the other minor characters though—like Clea’s best friend. I loved her!<br/>4/5<br/><br/>Dialogue- <br/>The dialogue was great. I really connected wit</span>
  <span id="freeText13647257331192041283" style="display:none">Elixir by Hillary Duff Book Review<br /><br />parafantasy.blogpsot.com<br /><br />Originality- <br />I liked the aspect of it being about immortality, but I felt like I’ve read something like it before. Like Evermore by Allison Noel. <br />3/5<br /><br />Characters- <br />I thought Clea was an okay protagonist. It was interesting to follow her side of the story but then again, I couldn’t really connect with her. <br />I loved the other minor characters though—like Clea’s best friend. I loved her!<br />4/5<br /><br />Dialogue- <br />The dialogue was great. I really connected with it, because as a teen I know what it’s like to read a forced attempt of an adult trying to sound like a teen—and there was none of that in this book. <br />5/5<br /><br />Plot-<br />The plot was very well planed out. I liked the twists and turns. The beginning felt a little slow to me, but when more characters start to come in the pace starts to pick back up again. The ending was kind of abrupt though. <br />3.5/5<br /><br />Setting-<br />The book had multiple settings. I never really got a good picture of the surroundings, but she did a good job of it towards the end of the book. <br />3/5<br /><br />Voice/writing- Hilary’s voice was great! I loved the fluidity of her words—it didn’t sound forced at all. And the grammar was just fine. <br />4/5<br /><br />Cover- I love the cover! The purple flower and the fonts are very eye-catching. <br />5/5<br /><br />Overall a 3.5/5<br />It was great but it didn’t really grab me much as a reader. That extra something wasn’t there that usually pulls me into the story—and I think that problem centers on originality. I recommend that you read it. Who knows, maybe it might interest you more than it did to me. It wasn’t a bad book. It’s just that it wasn’t the best either. <br /><br /></span>
